Note that it does not perform inheritance style merging.\n    30→// IOW, given three dest rules (*.foo.com, *.foo.com, *.com), calling this function for\n    31→// each config will result in a final dest rule set (*.foo.com, and *.com).\n    32→//\n    33→// The following is the merge logic:\n    34→// 1. Unique subsets (based on subset name) are concatenated to the original rule's list of subsets\n    35→// 2. If the original rule did not have any top level traffic policy, traffic policies from the new rule will be\n    36→// used.\n    37→// 3. If the original rule did not have any exportTo, exportTo settings from the new rule will be used.\n    38→func (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {\n    39→\trule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    40→\tresolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)\n    41→\tif mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n    42→\t\t// `addRuleToProcessedDestRules` determines if the incoming destination rule would become a new unique entry in the processedDestRules list.\n    43→\t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules := true\n    44→\t\tfor i, mdr := range mdrList {\n    45→\t\t\texistingRule := mdr.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    46→\t\t\tbothWithoutSelector := rule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil && existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil\n    47→\t\t\tbothWithSelector := existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil\n    48→\t\t\tselectorsMatch := labels.Instance(existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels()).Equals(rule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\n    49→\n    50→\t\t\tif bothWithSelector && !selectorsMatch {\n    51→\t\t\t\t// If the new destination rule and the existing one has workload selectors associated with them, skip merging\n    52→\t\t\t\t// if the selectors do not match\n    53→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n    54→\t\t\t}\n    55→\n    56→\t\t\t// If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\n    57→\t\t\t// If the incoming rule has a workload selector, it has to be merged with the existing rules with workload selector, and\n    58→\t\t\t// at the same time added as a unique entry in the processedDestRules.\n    59→\t\t\tif bothWithoutSelector || (rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && selectorsMatch) {\n    60→\t\t\t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules = false\n    61→\t\t\t}\n    62→\n    63→\t\t\t// Deep copy destination rule, to prevent mutate it later when merge with a new one.\n    64→\t\t\t// This can happen when there are more than one destination rule of same host in one namespace.\n    65→\t\t\tcopied := mdr.DeepCopy()\n    66→\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n    67→\t\t\tmergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    68→\n    69→\t\t\texistingSubset := map[string]struct{}{}\n    70→\t\t\tfor _, subset := range mergedRule.Subsets {\n    71→\t\t\t\texistingSubset[subset.Name] = struct{}{}\n    72→\t\t\t}\n    73→\t\t\t// we have an another destination rule for same host.\n    74→\t\t\t// concatenate both of them -- essentially add subsets from one to other.\n    75→\t\t\t// Note: we only add the subsets and do not overwrite anything else like exportTo or top level\n    76→\t\t\t// traffic policies if they already exist\n    77→\t\t\tfor _, subset := range rule.Subsets {\n    78→\t\t\t\tif _, ok := existingSubset[subset.Name]; !ok {\n    79→\t\t\t\t\t// if not duplicated, append\n    80→\t\t\t\t\tmergedRule.Subsets = append(mergedRule.Subsets, subset)\n    81→\t\t\t\t} else {\n    82→\t\t\t\t\t// duplicate subset\n    83→\t\t\t\t\tps.AddMetric(DuplicatedSubsets, string(resolvedHost), \"\",\n    84→\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Duplicate subset %s found while merging destination rules for %s\",\n    85→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tsubset.Name, string(resolvedHost)))\n    86→\t\t\t\t}\n    87→\t\t\t}\n    88→\n    89→\t\t\t// If there is no top level policy and the incoming rule has top level\n    90→\t\t\t// traffic policy, use the one from the incoming rule.\n    91→\t\t\tif mergedRule.TrafficPolicy == nil && rule.TrafficPolicy != nil {\n    92→\t\t\t\tmergedRule.TrafficPolicy = rule.TrafficPolicy\n    93→\t\t\t}\n    94→\t\t\t// If there is no exportTo in the existing rule and\n    95→\t\t\t// the incoming rule has an explicit exportTo, use the\n    96→\t\t\t// one from the incoming rule.\n    97→\t\t\tif len(p.exportTo[resolvedHost]) == 0 && len(exportToMap) > 0 {\n    98→\t\t\t\tp.exportTo[resolvedHost] = exportToMap\n    99→\t\t\t}\n   100→\t\t}\n   101→\t\tif addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n   102→\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n   103→\t\t}\n   104→\t\treturn\n   105→\t}\n   106→\t// DestinationRule does not exist for the resolved Note that it does not perform inheritance style merging.\n// IOW, given three dest rules (*.foo.com, *.foo.com, *.com), calling this function for\n// each config will result in a final dest rule set (*.foo.com, and *.com).\n//\n// The following is the merge logic:\n// 1. Unique subsets (based on subset name) are concatenated to the original rule's list of subsets\n// 2. If the original rule did not have any top level traffic policy, traffic policies from the new rule will be\n// used.\n// 3. If the original rule did not have any exportTo, exportTo settings from the new rule will be used.\nfunc (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {\n\trule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\tresolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)\n\tif mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n\t\t// `addRuleToProcessedDestRules` determines if the incoming destination rule would become a new unique entry in the processedDestRules list.\n\t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules := true\n\t\tfor i, mdr := range mdrList {\n\t\t\texistingRule := mdr.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\t\t\tbothWithoutSelector := rule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil && existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil\n\t\t\tbothWithSelector := existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil\n\t\t\tselectorsMatch := labels.Instance(existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels()).Equals(rule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\n\n\t\t\tif bothWithSelector && !selectorsMatch {\n\t\t\t\t// If the new destination rule and the existing one has workload selectors associated with them, skip merging\n\t\t\t\t// if the selectors do not match\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\n\t\t\t// If the incoming rule has a workload selector, it has to be merged with the existing rules with workload selector, and\n\t\t\t// at the same time added as a unique entry in the processedDestRules.\n\t\t\tif bothWithoutSelector || (rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && selectorsMatch) {\n\t\t\t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules = false\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Deep copy destination rule, to prevent mutate it later when merge with a new one.\n\t\t\t// This can happen when there are more than one destination rule of same host in one namespace.\n\t\t\tcopied := mdr.DeepCopy()\n\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n\t\t\tmergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\n\t\t\texistingSubset := map[string]struct{}{}\n\t\t\tfor _, subset := range mergedRule.Subsets {\n\t\t\t\texistingSubset[subset.Name] = struct{}{}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// we have an another destination rule for same host.\n\t\t\t// concatenate both of them -- essentially add subsets from one to other.\n\t\t\t// Note: we only add the subsets and do not overwrite anything else like exportTo or top level\n\t\t\t// traffic policies if they already exist\n\t\t\tfor _, subset := range rule.Subsets {\n\t\t\t\tif _, ok := existingSubset[subset.Name]; !ok {\n\t\t\t\t\t// if not duplicated, append\n\t\t\t\t\tmergedRule.Subsets = append(mergedRule.Subsets, subset)\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t// duplicate subset\n\t\t\t\t\tps.AddMetric(DuplicatedSubsets, string(resolvedHost), \"\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Duplicate subset %s found while merging destination rules for %s\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\tsubset.Name, string(resolvedHost)))\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// If there is no top level policy and the incoming rule has top level\n\t\t\t// traffic policy, use the one from the incoming rule.\n\t\t\tif mergedRule.TrafficPolicy == nil && rule.TrafficPolicy != nil {\n\t\t\t\tmergedRule.TrafficPolicy = rule.TrafficPolicy\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// If there is no exportTo in the existing rule and\n\t\t\t// the incoming rule has an explicit exportTo, use the\n\t\t\t// one from the incoming rule.\n\t\t\tif len(p.exportTo[resolvedHost]) == 0 && len(exportToMap) > 0 {\n\t\t\t\tp.exportTo[resolvedHost] = exportToMap\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\t// DestinationRule does not exist for the resolved host so add it\n\tp.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n\tp.exportTo[resolvedHost] = exportToMap\n}\n\n// inheritDestinationRule child config inherits settings from parent mesh/namespace\nfunc (ps *PushContext) inheritDestinationRule(parent, child *config.Config) *config.Config {\n\tif parent == nil {\n\t\treturn child\n\t}\n\tif child == nil {\n\t\treturn parent\n\t}\n\n\tparentDR := parent.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\tif parentDR.TrafficPolicy == nil {\n\t\treturn child\n\t}\n\n\tmerged := parent.DeepCopy()\n\t// merge child into parent, child fields will overwrite parent's\n\tproto.Merge(merged.Spec.(proto.Message), child.Spec.(proto.Message))\n\tmerged.Meta = services, virtualServices,\n    57→// and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n    58→// sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n    59→// for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n    60→// list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n    61→// SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n    62→// services. 310→\t\t\tfor _, p := range s.Ports {\n   311→\t\t\t\tfound := false\n   312→\t\t\t\tfor _, osp := range copied.Ports {\n   313→\t\t\t\t\tif p.Port == osp.Port {\n   314→\t\t\t\t\t\tfound = true\n   315→\t\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   316→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   317→\t\t\t\t}\n   318→\t\t\t\tif !found {\n   319→\t\t\t\t\tcopied.Ports = append(copied.Ports, p)\n   320→\t\t\t\t}\n   321→\t\t\t}\n   322→\t\t\t// replace service in slice\n   323→\t\t\tout.services[foundSvc.index] = copied\n   324→\t\t}\n   325→\t}\n   326→\n   327→\tfor _, listener := range out.EgressListeners {\n   328→\t\t// First add the explicitly requested services, which take priority\n   329→\t\tfor _, s := range listener.services {\n   330→\t\t\taddService(s)\n   331→\t\t}\n   332→\t\t// add dependencies on delegate virtual services\n   333→\t\tdelegates := ps.DelegateVirtualServicesConfigKey(listener.virtualServices)\n   334→\t\tfor _, delegate := range delegates {\n   335→\t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(delegate)\n   336→\t\t}\n   337→\n   338→\t\tmatchPort := needsPortMatch(listener)\n   339→\t\t// Infer more possible destinations from virtual services\n   340→\t\t// Services chosen here will not override services explicitly requested in listener.services.\n   341→\t\t// That way, if there is ambiguity around what hostname to pick, a user can specify the one they\n   342→\t\t// want in the hosts field, and the potentially random choice below won't matter\n   343→\t\tfor _, vs := range listener.virtualServices {\n   344→\t\t\tv := vs.Spec.(*networking.VirtualService)\n   345→\t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n   346→\t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.VirtualService,\n   347→\t\t\t\tName:      vs.Name,\n   348→\t\t\t\tNamespace: vs.Namespace,\n   349→\t\t\t})\n   350→\n   351→\t\t\tfor _, h := range virtualServiceDestinationHosts(v) {\n   352→\t\t\t\t// Default to this hostname in our config namespace\n   353→\t\t\t\tif s, ok := ps.ServiceIndex.HostnameAndNamespace[host.Name(h)][configNamespace]; ok {\n   354→\t\t\t\t\t// This won't overwrite hostnames that have already been found eg because they were requested in hosts\n   355→\t\t\t\t\tvar vss *Service\n   356→\t\t\t\t\tif matchPort {\n   357→\t\t\t\t\t\tvss = serviceMatchingListenerPort(s, listener)\n   358→\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n   359→\t\t\t\t\t\tvss = s\n   360→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   361→\t\t\t\t\tif vss != nil {\n   362→\t\t\t\t\t\taddService(vss)\n   363→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   364→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   365→\n   366→\t\t\t\t\t// We couldn't find the hostname in our config namespace\n   367→\t\t\t\t\t// We have to pick one arbitrarily for now, so we'll pick the first namespace alphabetically\n   368→\t\t\t\t\t// TODO: could we choose services more intelligently based on their ports?\n   369→\t\t\t\t\tbyNamespace := ps.ServiceIndex.HostnameAndNamespace[host.Name(h)]\n   370→\t\t\t\t\tif len(byNamespace) == 0 {\n   371→\t\t\t\t\t\t// This hostname isn't found anywhere\n   372→\t\t\t\t\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Could not find service hostname %s parsed from %s\", h, vs.Key())\n   373→\t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   374→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   375→\n   376→\t\t\t\t\tns := make([]string, 0, len(byNamespace))\n   377→\t\t\t\t\tfor k := range byNamespace {\n   378→\t\t\t\t\t\tif ps.IsServiceVisible(byNamespace[k], configNamespace) {\n   379→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tns = append(ns, k)\n   380→\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   381→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   382→\t\t\t\t\tif len(ns) > 0 {\n   383→\t\t\t\t\t\tsort.Strings(ns)\n   384→\t\t\t\t\t\t// Pick first namespace alphabetically\n   385→\t\t\t\t\t\t// This won't overwrite hostnames that have already been found eg because they were requested in hosts\n   386→\t\t\t\t\t\tvar vss *Service\n   387→\t\t\t\t\t\tif matchPort {\n   388→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tvss = serviceMatchingListenerPort(byNamespace[ns[0]], listener)\n   389→\t\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n   390→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tvss = byNamespace[ns[0]]\n   391→\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   392→\t\t\t\t\t\tif vss != nil {\n   393→\t\t\t\t\t\t\taddService(vss)\n   394→\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   395→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   396→\t\t\t\t}\n   397→\t\t\t}\n   398→\t\t}\n   399→\t}\n   400→\n   401→\t// Now that we have all the services that sidecars using this scope (in\n   402→\t// this config namespace) will see, identify all the destinationRules\n   403→\t// that these services need\n   404→\tout.servicesByHostname = make(map[host.Name]*Service, len(out.services))\n   405→\tout.destinationRules = make(map[host.Name][]*config.Config)\n   406→\tfor _, s := range out.services {\n   407→\t\tout.servicesByHostname[s.Hostname] = s\n   408→\t\tif drList := ps.destinationRule(configNamespace, s); drList != nil {\n   409→\t\t\tout.destinationRules[s.Hostname] = drList\n   410→\t\t\tfor _, dr := range drList {\n   411→\t\t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n   412→\t\t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n   413→\t\t\t\t\tName:      dr.Name,\n   414→\t\t\t\t\tNamespace: dr.Namespace,\n   415→\t\t\t\t})\n   416→\t\t\t}\n   417→\t\t}\n   418→\t}\n   419→\n   420→\tif sidecar.OutboundTrafficPolicy == nil {\n   421→\t\tif ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy != nil {\n   422→\t\t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = &networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy{\n   423→\t\t\t\tMode: networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy_Mode(ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy.Mode),\n   424→\t\t\t}\n   425→\t\t}\n   426→\t} else {\n   427→\t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = sidecar.OutboundTrafficPolicy\n   428→\t}\n   429→\n   430→\treturn out\n   431→}\n   432→\n   433→func convertIstioListenerToWrapper(ps *PushContext, configNamespace string,\n   434→\tistioListener *networking.IstioEgressListener) *IstioEgressListenerWrapper {\n   435→\tout := &IstioEgressListenerWrapper{\n   436→\t\tIstioListener: istioListener,\n   437→\t}\n   438→\n   439→\tout.listenerHosts = make(map[string][]host.Name)\n append(out.listenerHosts[parts[0]], host.Name(parts[1]))\n   453→\t}\n   454→\n   455→\tvses := ps.VirtualServicesForGateway(configNamespace, constants.IstioMeshGateway)\n   456→\tout.virtualServices = SelectVirtualServices(vses, out.listenerHosts)\n   457→\tsvces := ps.servicesExportedToNamespace(configNamespace)\n   458→\tout.services = out.selectServices(svces, configNamespace, out.listenerHosts)\n   459→\n   460→\treturn out\n   461→}\n   462→\n   463→// GetEgressListenerForRDS returns the egress listener corresponding to\n   464→// the listener port or the bind address or the catch all listener\n   465→func (sc *SidecarScope) GetEgressListenerForRDS(port int, bind string) *IstioEgressListenerWrapper {\n   466→\tif sc == nil {\n   467→\t\treturn nil\n   468→\t}\n   469→\n   470→\tfor _, e := range sc.EgressListeners {\n   471→\t\t// We hit a catchall listener. This is the last listener in the list of listeners\n   472→\t\t// return as is\n   473→\t\tif e.IstioListener == nil || e.IstioListener.Port == nil {\n   474→\t\t\treturn e\n   475→\t\t}\n   476→\n   477→\t\t// Check if the ports match\n   478→\t\t// for unix domain sockets (i.e. port == 0), check if the bind is equal to the routeName\n   479→\t\tif int(e.IstioListener.Port.Number) == port {\n   480→\t\t\tif port == 0 { // unix domain socket\n   481→\t\t\t\tif e.IstioListener.Bind == bind {\n   482→\t\t\t\t\treturn e\n   483→\t\t\t\t}\n   484→\t\t\t\t// no match.. continue searching\n   485→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   486→\t\t\t}\n   487→\t\t\t// this is a non-zero port match\n   488→\t\t\treturn e\n   489→\t\t}\n   490→\t}\n   491→\n   492→\t// This should never be reached unless user explicitly set an empty array for egress\n   493→\t// listeners which we actually forbid\n   494→\treturn nil\n   495→}\n   496→\n   497→// HasIngressListener returns if the sidecar scope has ingress (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n   524→\tif sc == nil {\n   525→\t\treturn true\n   526→\t}\n   527→\n   528→\t// This kind of config will trigger a change if made in the 538→\t_, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\n   539→\treturn exists\n   540→}\n   541→\n   542→// AddConfigDependencies add extra config dependencies to this scope. This action should be done before the\n   543→// SidecarScope being used to avoid concurrent read/write.\n   544→func (sc *SidecarScope) AddConfigDependencies(dependencies ...ConfigKey) {\n   545→\tif *SidecarScope) DestinationRule(direction TrafficDirection, proxy *Proxy, svc host.Name) *config.Config {\n   559→\tdestinationRules := sc.destinationRules[svc]\n   560→\tvar catchAllDr *config.Config\n   561→\tfor _, destRule := range destinationRules {\n   562→\t\tdestinationRule := destRule.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n   563→\t\tif destinationRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == only for outbound configuration, because\n   568→\t\t// for inbound configuration, the settings at sidecar would be more explicit and the preferred way forward.\n   569→\t\tif sc.Namespace == destRule.Namespace &&\n   570→\t\t\tdestinationRule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && direction == TrafficDirectionOutbound {\n   571→\t\t\tworkloadLabels := labels.Collection{proxy.Metadata.Labels}\n   572→\t\t\tworkloadSelector := labels.Instance(destinationRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\n   573→\t\t\t// return destination rule if workload selector matches\n   574→\t\t\tif portion of the Sidecar config.\n   592→// Note that the returned service could be trimmed.\n   593→func (ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) selectServices(services []*Service, configNamespace string, hosts map[string][]host.Name) []*Service {\n   594→\timportedServices := make([]*Service, 0)\n   595→\twildcardHosts, wnsFound := hosts[wildcardNamespace]\n   596→\tfor _, s := range services {\n   597→\t\tconfigNamespace := s.Attributes.Namespace\n   598→\n   599→\t\t// Check if there is an explicit import of form ns/* or ns/host\n   600→\t\tif importedHosts, nsFound := hosts[configNamespace]; nsFound {\n   601→\t\t\tif svc := matchingService(importedHosts, s, ilw); svc != nil {\n   602→\t\t\t\timportedServices = append(importedServices, svc)\n   603→\t\t\t}\n   604→\t\t} else if wnsFound { // Check if there is an import of form */host or */*\n   605→\t\t\tif svc := matchingService(wildcardHosts, s, ilw); svc != nil {\n   606→\t\t\t\timportedServices = append(importedServices, svc)\n   607→\t\t\t}\n   608→\t\t}\n   609→\t}\n   610→\n   611→\tvalidServices := make(map[host.Name]string)\n   612→\tfor _, svc := range importedServices {\n   613→\t\t_, f := validServices[svc.Hostname]\n in configNamespace, an arbitrary one will be chosen\n   617→\t\tif !f || svc.Attributes.Namespace == configNamespace {\n   618→\t\t\tvalidServices[svc.Hostname] = svc.Attributes.Namespace\n   619→\t\t}\n   620→\t}\n   621→\n   622→\tfilteredServices := make([]*Service, 0)\n   623→\t// Filter down to just instances in scope for the service\n   624→\tfor _, svc := range importedServices {\n 630→}\n   631→\n   632→// Return the original service or a trimmed service which has a subset of the ports in original service.\n   633→func matchingService(importedHosts []host.Name, service *Service, ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) *Service {\n   634→\tmatchPort := needsPortMatch(ilw)\n   635→\tfor _, importedHost := range importedHosts {\n   636→\t\t// Check if the hostnames match per usual hostname matching rules\n   637→\t\tif service.Hostname.SubsetOf(importedHost) {\n   638→\t\t\tif matchPort {\n   639→\t\t\t\treturn serviceMatchingListenerPort(service, ilw)\n   640→\t\t\t}\n   641→\t\t\treturn service\n   642→\t\t}\n   643→\t}\n   644→\treturn nil\n   645→}\n   646→\n   647→// serviceMatchingListenerPort constructs service with listener port.\n   648→func serviceMatchingListenerPort(service *Service, ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) *Service {\n   649→\tfor _, port := range service.Ports {\n   650→\t\tif port.Port == int(ilw.IstioListener.Port.GetNumber()) {\n   651→\t\t\tsc := service.DeepCopy()\n   652→\t\t\tsc.Ports = []*Port{port}\n   653→\t\t\treturn sc\n   654→\t\t}\n   655→\t}\n   656→\treturn nil\n   657→}\n   658→\n   659→func needsPortMatch(ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) bool {\n   660→\t// If a listener is defined with a port, we should match services with port except in the following case.\n   661→\t//  - If Port's protocol is proxy protocol(HTTP_PROXY) in which case the egress listener is used as generic egress http proxy.\n   662→\treturn ilw.IstioListener != nil && Sidecar resource with some\n// preprocessed data to determine the list of services, virtualServices,\n// and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n// sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n// for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n// list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n// SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n// services. The list of services seen by every sidecar scope (namespace\n// wide or per workload) depends on the imports, the listeners, and other\n// settings.\n//\n// Every proxy workload of SidecarProxy type will always map to a\n// SidecarScope object. If the proxy's namespace does not have a user\n// specified Sidecar CRD, we will construct one that has a catch all egress\n// listener that imports every public service/virtualService in the mesh.\ntype SidecarScope struct {\n\tName string\n\t// This is the namespace where the sidecar takes effect,\n\t// maybe different from the ns where sidecar resides if sidecar is in root ns.\n\tNamespace string\n\t// The crd itself. Can be nil if we are constructing the default\n\t// sidecar scope\n\tSidecar *networking.Sidecar\n\n\t// Version this sidecar was computed for\n\tVersion string\n\n\t// Set of egress listeners, and their associated services.  A sidecar\n\t// scope should have either ingress/egress listeners or both.  For\n\t// every proxy workload that maps to a sidecar API object (or the\n\t// default object), we will go through every egress listener in the\n\t// object and process the Envoy listener or RDS based on the imported\n\t// services/virtual services in that listener.\n\tEgressListeners []*IstioEgressListenerWrapper\n\n\t// Union of services imported across all egress listeners for use by CDS code.\n\tservices           []*Service\n\tservicesByHostname map[host.Name]*Service\n\n\t// Destination rules imported across all egress listeners. This\n\t// contains the computed set based on public/private destination rules\n\t// as well as the inherited ones, in addition to the wildcard matches\n\t// such as *.com applying to foo.bar.com. Each hostname in this map\n\t// corresponds to a service in the services array above. When computing\n\t// CDS, we simply have to find the matching service and return the\n\t// destination rule.\n\tdestinationRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config\n\t// OutboundTrafficPolicy defines the outbound traffic policy for this sidecar.\n\t// If OutboundTrafficPolicy is ALLOW_ANY traffic to unknown destinations will\n\t// be forwarded.\n\tOutboundTrafficPolicy *networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy\n\n\t// Set of known configs this sidecar depends on.\n\t// This field will be used to determine the config/resource scope\n\t// which means which config changes will affect the proxies within this scope.\n\tconfigDependencies map[uint64]struct{}\n\n\t// The namespace to treat as the administrative root namespace for\n\t// Istio configuration.\n\t//\n\t// Changes to Sidecar resources in this namespace will trigger a push.\n\tRootNamespace string\n}\n\n// MarshalJSON implements json.Marshaller\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) MarshalJSON() ([]byte, error) {\n\t// Json cannot expose unexported fields, so copy the ones we want here\n\treturn json.MarshalIndent(map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\"version\":               sc.Version,\n\t\t\"rootNamespace\":         sc.RootNamespace,\n\t\t\"name\":                  sc.Name,\n\t\t\"namespace\":             sc.Namespace,\n\t\t\"outboundTrafficPolicy\": sc.OutboundTrafficPolicy,\n\t\t\"services\":              sc.services,\n\t\t\"sidecar\":               sc.Sidecar,\n\t\t\"destinationRules\":      sc.destinationRules,\n\t}, \"\", \"  \")\n}\n\n// IstioEgressListenerWrapper is a wrapper for\n// networking.IstioEgressListener object. If we ignore this, then exportTo=. in\n\t\t// root namespace would always be ignored\n\t\tif hostname, ok := MostSpecificHostMatch(service.Hostname,\n\t\t\tps.destinationRuleIndex.rootNamespaceLocal.destRules,\n\t\t); ok {\n\t\t\treturn ps.destinationRuleIndex.rootNamespaceLocal.destRules[hostname]\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// 2. select destination rule from service namespace\n\tsvcNs := service.Attributes.Namespace\n\n\t// This can happen when finding the subset labels for a proxy in root namespace.\n\t// Because based on a pure cluster's fqdn, we do not know the service and\n\t// construct a fake service without setting Attributes at all.\n\tif svcNs == \"\" {\n\t\tfor _, svc := range ps.servicesExportedToNamespace(proxyNameSpace) {\n\t\t\tif service.Hostname == svc.Hostname && svc.Attributes.Namespace != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tsvcNs = svc.Attributes.Namespace\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// 3. if no private/public rule matched in the calling proxy's namespace,\n\t// check the target service's namespace for exported rules\n\tif svcNs != \"\" {\n\t\tif out := ps.getExportedDestinationRuleFromNamespace(svcNs, service.Hostname, proxyNameSpace); out != nil {\n\t\t\treturn out\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// 4. if no public/private rule in calling proxy's namespace matched, and no public rule in the\n\t// target service's namespace matched, search for any exported destination rule in the config root namespace\n\tif out := ps.getExportedDestinationRuleFromNamespace(ps.Mesh.RootNamespace, service.Hostname, proxyNameSpace); out != nil {\n\t\t\treturn []*config.Config{out}\n\t\t}\n\t\t// return mesh rule\n\t\tif out := ps.destinationRuleIndex.inheritedByNamespace[ps.Mesh.RootNamespace]; out != nil {\n\t\t\treturn []*config.Config{out}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (ps *PushContext) getExportedDestinationRuleFromNamespace(owningNamespace string, hostname host.Name, clientNamespace string) []*config.Config {\n\tif ps.destinationRuleIndex.exportedByNamespace[owningNamespace] != nil {\n\t\tif specificHostname, ok := MostSpecificHostMatch(hostname,\n\t\t\tps.destinationRuleIndex.exportedByNamespace[owningNamespace].destRules,\n\t\t); parent == nil {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tparent = ps.destinationRuleIndex.inheritedByNamespace[ps.Mesh.RootNamespace]\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\tvar inheritedDrList []*config.Config\n\t\t\t\t\tfor _, child := range ps.destinationRuleIndex.exportedByNamespace[owningNamespace].destRules[specificHostname] {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tinheritedDr := ps.inheritDestinationRule(parent, child)\n\t\t\t\t\t\tif inheritedDr != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\tinheritedDrList = append(inheritedDrList, inheritedDr)\n\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n","numLines":100,"startLine":990,"totalLines":2234}}}

Note that it does not perform inheritance style merging.\n    30→// IOW, given three dest rules (*.foo.com, *.foo.com, *.com), calling this function for\n    31→// each config will result in a final dest rule set (*.foo.com, and *.com).\n    32→//\n    33→// The following is the merge logic:\n    34→// 1. Unique subsets (based on subset name) are concatenated to the original rule's list of subsets\n    35→// 2. If the original rule did not have any top level traffic policy, traffic policies from the new rule will be\n    36→// used.\n    37→// 3. If the original rule did not have any exportTo, exportTo settings from the new rule will be used.\n    38→func (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {\n    39→\trule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    40→\tresolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)\n    41→\tif mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n    42→\t\t// `addRuleToProcessedDestRules` determines if the incoming destination rule would become a new unique entry in the processedDestRules list.\n    43→\t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules := true\n    44→\t\tfor i, mdr := range mdrList {\n    45→\t\t\texistingRule := mdr.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    46→\t\t\tbothWithoutSelector := rule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil && existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil\n    47→\t\t\tbothWithSelector := existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil\n    48→\t\t\tselectorsMatch := labels.Instance(existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels()).Equals(rule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\n    49→\n    50→\t\t\tif bothWithSelector && !selectorsMatch {\n    51→\t\t\t\t// If the new destination rule and the existing one has workload selectors associated with them, skip merging\n    52→\t\t\t\t// if the selectors do not match\n    53→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n    54→\t\t\t}\n    55→\n    56→\t\t\t// If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\n    57→\t\t\t// If the incoming rule has a workload selector, it has to be merged with the existing rules with workload selector, and\n    58→\t\t\t// at the same time added as a unique entry in the processedDestRules.\n    59→\t\t\tif bothWithoutSelector || (rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && selectorsMatch) {\n    60→\t\t\t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules = false\n    61→\t\t\t}\n    62→\n    63→\t\t\t// Deep copy destination rule, to prevent mutate it later when merge with a new one.\n    64→\t\t\t// This can happen when there are more than one destination rule of same host in one namespace.\n    65→\t\t\tcopied := mdr.DeepCopy()\n    66→\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n    67→\t\t\tmergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    68→\n    69→\t\t\texistingSubset := map[string]struct{}{}\n    70→\t\t\tfor _, subset := range mergedRule.Subsets {\n    71→\t\t\t\texistingSubset[subset.Name] = struct{}{}\n    72→\t\t\t}\n    73→\t\t\t// we have an another destination rule for same host.\n    74→\t\t\t// concatenate both of them -- essentially add subsets from one to other.\n    75→\t\t\t// Note: we only add the subsets and do not overwrite anything else like exportTo or top level\n    76→\t\t\t// traffic policies if they already exist\n    77→\t\t\tfor _, subset := range rule.Subsets {\n    78→\t\t\t\tif _, ok := existingSubset[subset.Name]; !ok {\n    79→\t\t\t\t\t// if not duplicated, append\n    80→\t\t\t\t\tmergedRule.Subsets = append(mergedRule.Subsets, subset)\n    81→\t\t\t\t} else {\n    82→\t\t\t\t\t// duplicate subset\n    83→\t\t\t\t\tps.AddMetric(DuplicatedSubsets, string(resolvedHost), \"\",\n    84→\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Duplicate subset %s found while merging destination rules for %s\",\n    85→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tsubset.Name, string(resolvedHost)))\n    86→\t\t\t\t}\n    87→\t\t\t}\n    88→\n    89→\t\t\t// If there is no top level policy and the incoming rule has top level\n    90→\t\t\t// traffic policy, use the one from the incoming rule.\n    91→\t\t\tif mergedRule.TrafficPolicy == nil && rule.TrafficPolicy != nil {\n    92→\t\t\t\tmergedRule.TrafficPolicy = rule.TrafficPolicy\n    93→\t\t\t}\n    94→\t\t\t// If there is no exportTo in the existing rule and\n    95→\t\t\t// the incoming rule has an explicit exportTo, use the\n    96→\t\t\t// one from the incoming rule.\n    97→\t\t\tif len(p.exportTo[resolvedHost]) == 0 && len(exportToMap) > 0 {\n    98→\t\t\t\tp.exportTo[resolvedHost] = exportToMap\n    99→\t\t\t}\n   100→\t\t}\n   101→\t\tif addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n   102→\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n   103→\t\t}\n   104→\t\treturn\n   105→\t}\n   106→\t// DestinationRule does not exist for the resolved host so add it\n   107→\tp.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n   108→\tp.exportTo[resolvedHost] = exportToMap\n   109→}\n   110→\n   111→// {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01MYrPcM5uEU3fLg22wpgAha","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01UUrPVJibPTqTfoN7sYZ7Zb","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update\n\n## Summary\n\nWhen multiple DestinationRules for the same host are merged during PushContext initialization, only the metadata (name/namespace) of the first DR is retained in the consolidated structure. Consequently, when SidecarScope builds config dependencies, only that one DR's ConfigKey is registered. When the second (or other contributing) DR is updated later, its ConfigKey is not found in the sidecar's `configDependencies`, causing `DependsOnConfig()` to return false and the xDS push to be incorrectly skipped.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` line 38-109, specifically the `mergeDestinationRule()` function in conjunction with dependency tracking in `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` lines 219-227 and 410-416.\n\n**Mechanism**:\n1. When `mergeDestinationRule()` merges multiple DRs for the same host, the function modifies the first matching DR in-place by appending subsets and traffic policies from the incoming DR\n2. The consolidated entry in `destRules[resolvedHost]` contains merged spec from both DRs but retains **only** the metadata (Name/Namespace) of the first DR\n3. When `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterate over `destinationRules` to register dependencies, they call `AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: dr.Name, Namespace: dr.Namespace})` only for the DRs that exist in the consolidated list\n4. Since the second DR was merged into the first and not added as a separate entry, its ConfigKey is never registered\n5. When the second DR is updated, `ConfigAffectsProxy()` calls `DependsOnConfig()` with the second DR's ConfigKey, which returns false (not in `configDependencies`), and the push is skipped\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Merge Process in destination_rule.go\n\n**File**: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`\n\nThe `mergeDestinationRule()` function handles multiple DRs for the same host:\n\n```go\nfunc (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {\n\trule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\tresolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)\n\tif mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n\t\t// Line 43-44: Loop through existing merged destination rules\n\t\tfor i, mdr := range mdrList {\n\t\t\texistingRule := mdr.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\t\t\t// ... selector matching logic ...\n\n\t\t\t// Line 65-66: Deep copy the FIRST matched DR and modify it in place\n\t\t\tcopied := mdr.DeepCopy()\n\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n\t\t\tmergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\n\t\t\t// Line 77-87: Append subsets from incoming DR to the first DR\n\t\t\tfor _, subset := range rule.Subsets {\n\t\t\t\tif _, ok := existingSubset[subset.Name]; !ok {\n\t\t\t\t\tmergedRule.Subsets = append(mergedRule.Subsets, subset)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// ... continue with traffic policy merging ...\n\t\t}\n\t\t// Line 101-103: If addRuleToProcessedDestRules is false (merge happened),\n\t\t// the incoming DR is NOT added to the list\n\t\tif addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n\t\t\tp.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\t// ...\n}\n```\n\n**Critical observation**: After merging, `destRules[resolvedHost]` contains only ONE config.Config entry (the modified first DR). The second DR's subsets are merged into this entry, but the second DR itself is not stored in the consolidated list. **The Name and Namespace of the second DR are lost**.\n\n### 2. Consequently, only DR-1's metadata survives in the consolidated structure, and only `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-traffic-policy\"}` is registered in `configDependencies`, NOT `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\"}`\n\n8. **Result**: When DR-2 is updated, `DependsOnConfig()` is called with `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\"}`, which was never registered, so the hash lookup at `sidecar.go:538` fails, returns false, and the proxy is excluded from the push\n\n9. **Final Outcome**: Envoy sidecar does not receive xDS update and continues serving stale cluster and route configuration; operator must restart the pod to trigger a full rebuild\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Cause Fix\nThe fundamental issue is the loss of identity metadata during DestinationRule consolidation. There are several potential fix strategies:\n\n**Option 1 (Recommended): Track All Contributing DRs**\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of all contributing DR metadata, not just the consolidated spec\n- When registering dependencies in SidecarScope, iterate over ALL contributing DRs and register each one's ConfigKey\n- This ensures that updates to ANY contributing DR trigger a push\n\n**Option 2: Hash-based Dependency Tracking**\n- Instead of registering ConfigKey by (Name, Namespace), register a hash of the resolved host\n- When a DestinationRule for that host is updated, check if it matches the host before filtering\n- Less precise but avoids metadata loss\n\n**Option 3: Separate Registry for Merged Config Origins**\n- Maintain a separate map `mergedConfigOrigins: map[host.Name][]ConfigKey` that tracks which original DRs were merged to create each consolidated entry\n- When pushing, expand the ConfigsUpdated set to include all origins before calling `DependsOnConfig()`\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n1. Enable debug logging in `sidecar.go:AddConfigDependencies()` to log all registered ConfigKeys\n2. Compare registered ConfigKeys with actual DestinationRules in the cluster\n3. Verify that after merging, the consolidated list contains entries for BOTH contributing DRs (or at least metadata for both)\n4. Add validation in `mergeDestinationRule()` to warn if consolidation results in loss of metadata\n\n### Test Cases to Add\n1. Create two DRs for the same host (one with subsets, one with traffic policy)\n2. Update the DR that was \"lost\" in consolidation\n3. Verify that the sidecar receives an xDS push\n4. Check that `configDependencies` contains ConfigKeys for both DRs\n\n### Longer-term Improvements\n- Consider deprecating the implicit merging behavior and requiring users to define a single DR per host with all subsets and policies\n- Document the consolidation semantics more clearly in API and implementation comments\n- Add metrics to track how many DRs are consolidated per host to aid observability\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2123,"cache_read_input_tokens":52488,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2123},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ebd8ce57-63fc-4fc7-b6b1-6a51c9d56e40","uuid":"168547a3-37a0-43ac-a510-c2bb0cb6e0e0"}

Consequently, when SidecarScope builds config dependencies, only that one DR's ConfigKey is registered. When the second (or other contributing) DR is updated later, its ConfigKey is not found in the sidecar's `configDependencies`, causing `DependsOnConfig()` to return false and the xDS push to be incorrectly skipped.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` line 38-109, specifically the `mergeDestinationRule()` function in conjunction with dependency tracking in `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` lines 219-227 and 410-416.\n\n**Mechanism**:\n1. When `mergeDestinationRule()` merges multiple DRs for the same host, the function modifies the first matching DR in-place by appending subsets and traffic policies from the incoming DR\n2. The consolidated entry in `destRules[resolvedHost]` contains merged spec from both DRs but retains **only** the metadata (Name/Namespace) of the first DR\n3. When `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterate over `destinationRules` to register dependencies, they call `AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: dr.Name, Namespace: dr.Namespace})` only for the DRs that exist in the consolidated list\n4. Since the second DR was merged into the first and not added as a separate entry, its ConfigKey is never registered\n5. When the second DR is updated, `ConfigAffectsProxy()` calls `DependsOnConfig()` with the second DR's ConfigKey, which returns false (not in `configDependencies`), and the push is skipped\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. The second DR's subsets are merged into this entry, but the second DR itself is not stored in the consolidated list. **The Name and Namespace of the second DR are lost**.\n\n### 2. `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 254-431)\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` (lines 523-540)\n   - `AddConfigDependencies()` (lines 542-555)\n   - `configDependencies` field in `SidecarScope` (line 110)\n\n4. **pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (lines 32-58)\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` (lines 60-74)\n\n5. **pilot/pkg/bootstrap/server.go**\n   - `initRegistryEventHandlers()` (lines 863-915)\n   - Config change event handler (lines 881-903)\n   - Populates `ConfigsUpdated` in PushRequest\n\n6. **pilot/pkg/config/config.go**\n   - `ConfigKey` type (lines 54-58)\n   - `HashCode()` method (lines 60-69)\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Operator updates DR-2 (reviews-subsets) adding a v3 subset, but Envoy sidecar does not receive updated xDS config\n\n2. **→ Intermediate Hop 1**: When DR-2 is updated in the Kubernetes API server, config controller in `bootstrap/server.go:881` detects the change and creates a PushRequest with ConfigsUpdated containing DR-2's ConfigKey: `{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n\n3. **→ Intermediate Hop 2**: The xDS layer calls `ConfigAffectsProxy()` in `proxy_dependencies.go:32` to determine if the proxy needs a push, passing the DR-2 ConfigKey\n\n4. **→ Intermediate Hop 3**: `checkProxyDependencies()` at line 60 calls `proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(dr2_configkey)`, which checks if DR-2's ConfigKey is in the sidecar's `configDependencies` map\n\n5. **→ Intermediate Hop 4**: During initial SidecarScope construction (in `sidecar.go:219-227` or `410-416`), the dependency registration loop iterates over merged destination rules returned by `ps.destinationRule()`, which has consolidated DR-1 and DR-2 into a single entry\n\n6. **→ Intermediate Hop 5**: The merged entry in `consolidatedDestRules.destRules[hostname]` contains only ONE `config.Config` object with the Name=\"reviews-traffic-policy\" and Namespace=\"default\" (the first DR that was stored before merging)\n\n7. **→ Root Cause**: In `destination_rule.go:38-109`, when `mergeDestinationRule()` was called for DR-2 after DR-1 was already in the consolidated list, it modified the first DR in-place (line 66) and appended DR-2's subsets to it (lines 77-87), but did NOT add DR-2 as a separate entry in the list (line 101). Consequently, only DR-1's metadata survives in the consolidated structure, and only `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-traffic-policy\"}` is registered in `configDependencies`, NOT `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\"}`\n\n8. **Result**: When DR-2 is updated, `DependsOnConfig()` is called with `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\"}`, which was never registered, so the hash lookup at `sidecar.go:538` fails, returns false, and the proxy is excluded from the push\n\n9. **Final Outcome**: Envoy sidecar does not receive xDS update and continues serving stale cluster and route configuration; operator must restart the pod to trigger a full rebuild\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Cause Fix\nThe fundamental issue is the loss of identity metadata during DestinationRule consolidation. There are several potential fix strategies:\n\n**Option 1 (Recommended): Track All Contributing DRs**\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of all contributing DR metadata, not just the consolidated spec\n- When registering dependencies in SidecarScope, iterate over ALL contributing DRs and register each one's ConfigKey\n- This ensures that updates to ANY contributing DR trigger a push\n\n**Option 2: Hash-based Dependency Tracking**\n- Instead of registering ConfigKey by (Name, Namespace), register a hash of the resolved host\n- When a DestinationRule for that host is updated, check if it matches the host before filtering\n- Less precise but avoids metadata loss\n\n**Option 3: Separate Registry for Merged Config Origins**\n- Maintain a separate map `mergedConfigOrigins: map[host.Name][]ConfigKey` that tracks which original DRs were merged to create each consolidated entry\n- When pushing, expand the ConfigsUpdated set to include all origins before calling `DependsOnConfig()`\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n1. Enable debug logging in `sidecar.go:AddConfigDependencies()` to log all registered ConfigKeys\n2. Compare registered ConfigKeys with actual DestinationRules in the cluster\n3. Verify that after merging, the consolidated list contains entries for BOTH contributing DRs (or at least metadata for both)\n4. Add validation in `mergeDestinationRule()` to warn if consolidation results in loss of metadata\n\n### Test Cases to Add\n1. Create two DRs for the same host (one with subsets, one with traffic policy)\n2. Update the DR that was \"lost\" in consolidation\n3. Verify that the sidecar receives an xDS push\n4. Check that `configDependencies` contains ConfigKeys for both DRs\n\n### Longer-term Improvements\n- Consider deprecating the implicit merging behavior and requiring users to define a single DR per host with all subsets and policies\n- Document the consolidation semantics more clearly in API and implementation comments\n- Add metrics to track how many DRs are consolidated per host to aid observability\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
